# Microsoft 365 Teams Administrator Associate Cert Prep (MS-700): Managing Collaboration Tools

> The collaboration and communication that Microsoft Teams enables can be an invaluable tool for businesses, as shown by the exponential growth of Microsoft Teams usage during the pandemic. But how can you administer meetings and policies effectively? Instructor Robert McMillen shows you how to manage everything Microsoft Teams has to offer, including chats, collaboration, meetings, phone systems, a

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools) | 2h 4m | Intermediate | 20K learners

## Instructor

- [[Robert McMillen]]

## Skills Covered

- Microsoft Teams

#### Manage external access
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] With Microsoft Teams external access, Teams users from other domains can connect with you in your Teams, chats, and calls.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=8)** You can also allow other external users who are still using Skype for Business Online or Skype for Business Server.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=14)** You should use external access, however, when you have users in different domains in your business, for example, if you had Rob@[contoso.com](https://contoso.com) and Ann@[northwindtraders.com](https://northwindtraders.com), and you want anyone else in the world who uses Teams to be able to find and contact you using just your email address.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=32)** Now, this only works, of course, if you have an email address that is licensed for Teams, and you must both enable external access in order to be found.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=43)** There's several different scenarios where we can configure external access for organizations.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=49)** The first one would be when you can use open Federation.

> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=53)** And this is the default setting and it lets people in your organization find, call, and send IMs chats as well as set up other meetings with people external to your organization.

> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=71)** The next scenario would be you can add a domain or domains to the allow list.

> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=76)** To do this, you've got to click Add a domain, then add the domain name, click Action, to take on this domain, and then select it to be allowed.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=85)** And the last one would be you can add a domain or domains to the block list.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=90)** To do this, you add a domain, add the domain name, click the action to take, and then click Blocked.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=96)** It's important to know that if you do this it will allow all of the domains, whereas the second option will do the opposite, it will block all domains except the ones you allow.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=107)** I'm in the Teams admin center and I'm going to expand Users, and then click on External access.

>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=179)** Once I have everything set the way I want it, I can click Save, and now our external access policy is complete.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-external-access?u=76281980&t=186)** External access policies are a quick way to decide what domains you would like to communicate with and what domains may be blocked.

#### Manage channels for a team
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-channels-for-a-team?u=76281980)

#### Manage call park policies

#### Interpret a dial plan
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Dial plans in Microsoft Teams.
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=2)** So what is a dial plan?
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=4)** A dial plan is a name set of normalization rules that translate dialed phone numbers by an individual user, into an alternate format.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=14)** Typically, you're going to see E.164.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=17)** And E.164 is just a way to make sure that every phone number has its own unique address because you don't want to have two different locations with the same phone number.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=28)** And this is all for purposes of call authorization and voice routing.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=32)** A dial plan consists of one or more normalization rules that's going to define how phone numbers expressed in various formats are translated into that alternate format.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=42)** And there can be a maximum of 1000 tenant dial plans, so most likely you'll never hit that amount.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=50)** If you have clients, a dial plan scope determines the hierarchical level at which the dial plan can be applied.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=58)** Clients are going to get the appropriate dial plan through provisioning settings, and they're automatically provided when a user signs into Teams.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=66)** You can manage dial plan scope settings by using the Microsoft Teams admin center or remote PowerShell.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=74)** Now in Teams, there are two different types of dial plans.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=76)** There's service scoped and tenant scoped.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=79)** A service scope dial plan is defined for every country or region where a phone system is available.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-a-dial-plan?u=76281980&t=85)** As clients are provisioned, they're going to obtain what's called an effective dial plan.
>

#### Interpret the Health Dashboard for Direct Routing
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The Direct Routing Health Dashboard can help you monitor the connection between your Session Border Controller, SBC, and the Direct Routing interface.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=9)** A voice session border controller is a device regularly deployed in VoIP networks, and we use that to control the signaling and also the media streams involved in setting up and tearing down telephone calls.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=23)** The dashboard can provide information on potential issues, such as reasons why you get dropped calls, as well as the status of the connected SBCs, and that includes detailed information on the SBCs and their overall health.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=37)** The information regarding overall health of the connected SBCs includes a direct routing summary and network effectiveness, which compares the number of calls sent versus the number of calls delivered to a recipient.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=52)** Then there's the Network Effectiveness Ratio, that's also referred to as the NER, and that measures the ability of networks to deliver calls to the far end terminal, therefore, when recipients reject a call, the call will be considered a successful delivery.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=67)** It means that an answer message, a busy signal, or a ring with no answer are all considered successful calls.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=74)** And then there's the average call duration, and this parameter can help you to monitor the quality of calls.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=79)** The average duration of a one-to-one public switch telephone network call is around four to five minutes, but this average can differ in different companies, so it's recommended that you establish a baseline for the average call duration for your organization, because if the parameter falls much lower below the baseline, it's going to indicate your users are having issues with call quality.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=102)** Then there's the Transport Layer Security connectivity status, also known as the TLS status.

> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=228)** Jitter is the millisecond measure of delay time between two endpoints using the RTP control protocol.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=235)** Packet loss is going to be a measure of packets that failed to arrive, which is going to be computed between two computers or two endpoints.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=243)** Latency is the amount of time that it takes for a signal to be sent plus the length of time it takes for that signal to be received.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/interpret-the-health-dashboard-for-direct-routing?u=76281980&t=251)** The health dashboard gives us a high level view of what's happening in our calls and if any action needs to take place.

#### Manage access review for team members
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-access-review-for-team-members?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>

### 7. Implement Policies for Microsoft Teams Apps

#### Manage organization-wide app settings
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-organization-wide-app-settings?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-organization-wide-app-settings?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] You can use org-wide app settings to control whether users can install third-party apps and whether users can upload or interact with custom apps in your Teams tenant.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-organization-wide-app-settings?u=76281980&t=11)** Org-wide app settings govern the behavior for all users and they override any other app permission policies assigned to them.

> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-organization-wide-app-settings?u=76281980&t=100)** If I made any changes, you could see the Save button light up, but I didn't, so I'm just going to go ahead and click Cancel and then we can continue on with managing apps.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/manage-organization-wide-app-settings?u=76281980&t=110)** A good thing about these org-wide settings is that if you suspect an app is malicious, but you're not sure which one, you can disable all of them from the org-wide app settings and then figure out the app in question afterwards.

> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/troubleshoot-audio-video-and-client-issues?u=76281980&t=98)** If you're having an issue with your camera showing up, it could be because there's another app using it.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/troubleshoot-audio-video-and-client-issues?u=76281980&t=103)** And you can use the test settings in Teams to make a call.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/troubleshoot-audio-video-and-client-issues?u=76281980&t=107)** When you go into a Team meeting, you can also test your video as well as your audio.
>

>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/troubleshoot-audio-video-and-client-issues?u=76281980&t=129)** We can also close other applications if resources are low.

>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/troubleshoot-audio-video-and-client-issues?u=76281980&t=156)** Troubleshooting in Teams usually has a simple solution.

>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-managing-collaboration-tools/troubleshoot-microsoft-teams-sign-in-issues?u=76281980&t=7)** So, you can see this first code in the upper left is you ran into an authorization problem.

>
